href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></li><li>Certified Hitmakers<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #b0c4de"></th></tr><tr><th <p><b>Lathan Moses Stanley Echols</b> (born January 25, 2002), known professionally as <b>Lil Mosey</b>, is an American rapper, singer, and songwriter. He rose to fame in late 2017 with the release of his single "Pull Up". Mosey's debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Northsbest" title="Northsbest">Northsbest</a></i> (2018) included his first <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> charting single, "<a href="/wiki/Noticed_(song)" title="Noticed (song)">Noticed</a>". His second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Certified_Hitmaker" title="Certified Hitmaker">Certified Hitmaker</a></i> (2019), peaked at number 12 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, and contains his 2019 hit single "<a href="/wiki/Stuck_in_a_Dream" title="Stuck in a Dream">Stuck in a Dream</a>". In 2020, Mosey released the highest-charting song of his career, "<a href="/wiki/Blueberry_Faygo" title="Blueberry Faygo">Blueberry Faygo</a>", which peaked at number 8 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.
</p><p>In April 2021, Mosey was charged with <a href="/wiki/Rape_laws_in_the_United_States" title="Rape laws in the United States">second degree rape</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lewis_County,_Washington" title="Lewis County, Washington">Lewis County, Washington</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The trial began on February 22, 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-February_16_trial_date_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-February_16_trial_date-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> On March 3, 2023, Mosey was found <a href="/wiki/Acquittal" title="Acquittal">not guilty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lathan Moses Stanley Echols was born on January 25, 2002, in <a href="/wiki/Mountlake_Terrace,_Washington" title="Mountlake Terrace, Washington">Mountlake Terrace, Washington</a>, to a white mother and a half-Puerto Rican, half-black father.<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Revolt_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Revolt-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He was raised by his mother in the north side of <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>. He began rapping in his early teens and started his music career in the eighth grade. Echols first attended <a href="/wiki/Mountlake_Terrace_High_School" title="Mountlake Terrace High School">Mountlake Terrace High School</a>, then transferred to <a href="/wiki/Shorecrest_High_School" title="Shorecrest High School">Shorecrest High School</a> in the tenth grade. He later dropped out of school following the success of his song "Pull Up", and went on to pursue his career, heading to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> to record.<sup id="cite_ref-AllMusic_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Revolt_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Revolt-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="2016.E2.80.932018:_Career_beginnings_and_Northsbest"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–2018:_Career_beginnings_and_Northsbest">2016–2018: Career beginnings and <i>Northsbest</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2016–2018: Career beginnings and Northsbest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2016, Lil Mosey uploaded his first song, titled "So Bad", to the music streaming service <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud" title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a>, quickly receiving 50,000 views, which acted as the lead single for his 2017 mixtape <i>Northsbest</i>. As of August 2023 "So Bad" has accumulated 34.3 Million streams on SoundCloud. On November 13, 2016, Mosey competed and placed fourth at the Coast 2 Coast Live Seattle All Ages Edition. 
</p><p>"Pull Up" was Mosey's first released track and served as his debut commercial single.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Its music video reached over 25 million views on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> in the first 16 months upon its release.<sup id="cite_ref-ST1_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ST1-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> On March 14, 2018, Mosey released his second commercial single "Boof Pack". Its music video was released on the <a href="/wiki/WorldStarHipHop" title="WorldStarHipHop">WorldStarHipHop</a> channel, and received over 13 million views on YouTube in just over a year after its release.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Around four months later, he released "<a href="/wiki/Noticed_(song)" title="Noticed (song)">Noticed</a>" as his third commercial single alongside a music video directed by <a href="/wiki/Cole_Bennett" title="Cole Bennett">Cole Bennett</a>. The song peaked at number 80 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, while its music video has gone on to become one of the most popular videos on Lyrical Lemonade, amassing almost 290 million views to date.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In the video, "Mosey and his friends live the good life as they relax in a luxury apartment, which overlooks a beautiful beach".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> His fourth single, "<a href="/wiki/Yoppa_(song)" title="Yoppa (song)">Yoppa</a>", was released on October 4, featuring fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/BlocBoy_JB" title="BlocBoy JB">BlocBoy JB</a>.
</p><p>On October 19, 2018, Mosey released his debut studio album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Northsbest" title="Northsbest">Northsbest</a></i>, which includes the four previously released singles and seven other tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The album's opening track, <i><a href="/wiki/Kamikaze_(Lil_Mosey_song)" title="Kamikaze (Lil Mosey song)">Kamikaze</a></i>, was supported by a Lyrical Lemonade music video four days after its release, boosting its popularity and peaking at number 97 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. The music video has over 80 million views to date. On December 7, Mosey released a standalone single, "K for Christmas".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2019:_Certified_Hitmaker">2019: <i>Certified Hitmaker</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2019: Certified Hitmaker">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mosey started off 2019 by releasing the single "Bust Down Cartier" on March 15. Produced by Mosey himself, it was added to the re-release of his debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Northsbest" title="Northsbest">Northsbest</a></i>, titled <i>Northsbest (Extended)</i>, with that being the only additional song. The song was supported by a <a href="/wiki/Cole_Bennett" title="Cole Bennett">Cole Bennett</a>-directed music video on Lyrical Lemonade, garnering over 15 million views to date. Three months later, he released "G Walk", the lead single for his upcoming second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Certified_Hitmaker" title="Certified Hitmaker">Certified Hitmaker</a></i>. The song features American singer <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown" title="Chris Brown">Chris Brown</a>. This was followed up by "<a href="/wiki/Stuck_in_a_Dream" title="Stuck in a Dream">Stuck in a Dream</a>" on September 17, featuring fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Gunna_(rapper)" title="Gunna (rapper)">Gunna</a>. The song peaked at number 62 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, overtaking the number 80 peak of "Noticed". The song's music video, which premiered on Mosey's official <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel on the same day, has amassed over 45 million views to date. On November 5, Mosey released the album's third single, "Live This Wild", accompanied by a music video released a week later. Although it did not chart on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, it managed to peak at number 80 on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a>. The music video has over 25 million views.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Certified_Hitmaker" title="Certified Hitmaker">Certified Hitmaker</a></i> was released three days later on November 8, 2019, containing the three singles and eleven other tracks. <sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The album features additional guest appearances from rappers <a href="/wiki/Trippie_Redd" title="Trippie Redd">Trippie Redd</a> and <a href="/wiki/AJ_Tracey" title="AJ Tracey">AJ Tracey</a>. On November 22, Mosey was featured on "This Ain't That", the sixth track on American rapper <a href="/wiki/Trippie_Redd" title="Trippie Redd">Trippie Redd</a>'s fourth commercial mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/A_Love_Letter_to_You_4" title="A Love Letter to You 4">A Love Letter to You 4</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span id="2020:_Rise_to_mainstream_popularity_with_.22Blueberry_Faygo.22_and_feature_run"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020:_Rise_to_mainstream_popularity_with_&quot;Blueberry_Faygo&quot;_and_feature_run">2020: Rise to mainstream popularity with "Blueberry Faygo" and feature run</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2020: Rise to mainstream popularity with &quot;Blueberry Faygo&quot; and feature run">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On January 31, 2020, Mosey was featured on "Safe With Me", a song from Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Eladio_Carri%C3%B3n" title="Eladio Carrión">Eladio Carrión</a>'s debut studio album <i>Sauce Boyz</i>. On February 7, 2020, Mosey released the single "<a href="/wiki/Blueberry_Faygo" title="Blueberry Faygo">Blueberry Faygo</a>", after it garnered traction and went viral after being leaked on streaming platform <a href="/wiki/Spotify" title="Spotify">Spotify</a> throughout 2019. The song debuted at number 62 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, tying with "Stuck in a Dream". It later became his highest-peaking song on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, peaking at number 8 and charting well internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Certified_Hitmaker" title="Certified Hitmaker">Certified Hitmaker</a></i> was reissued on the same day to include "Blueberry Faygo", the only addition on the tracklist. The song's music video premiered a month later on Lyrical Lemonade, and has amassed almost 300 million views since then. It has also gone on to become one of the most viewed music videos on the channel, together with "Noticed". This was notably Mosey's fourth collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Cole_Bennett" title="Cole Bennett">Cole Bennett</a>, after 2018's "Noticed" and "Kamikaze", and 2019's "Bust Down Cartier".
</p><p>On March 11, Mosey was featured on Jamaican record producer <a href="/wiki/Rvssian" title="Rvssian">Rvssian</a>'s single "Only The Team", which also features fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Tjay" title="Lil Tjay">Lil Tjay</a>. On June 19, Mosey was featured on Canadian singer <a href="/wiki/Tate_McRae" title="Tate McRae">Tate McRae</a>'s song "vicious". Five days later on June 24, Mosey was featured on "WRONG", the third track on Australian rapper <a href="/wiki/The_Kid_LAROI" class="mw-redirect" title="The Kid LAROI">The Kid LAROI</a>'s debut commercial mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/F*ck_Love" title="F*ck Love">F*ck Love</a></i>. The song's music video, directed by American social media personality <a href="/wiki/Logan_Paul" title="Logan Paul">Logan Paul</a>, premiered on September 18 and has been viewed over 60 million times. "WRONG" peaked at number 9 on the US <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_the_Hot_100" class="mw-redirect" title="Bubbling Under the Hot 100">Bubbling Under the Hot 100</a> and number 98 on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a>. On June 26, Mosey released the song "Back at It", featuring fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Baby" title="Lil Baby">Lil Baby</a>, as the first single of the deluxe edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Certified_Hitmaker" title="Certified Hitmaker">Certified Hitmaker</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Uproxx_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uproxx-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The song charted at number 9 on the US <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_the_Hot_100" class="mw-redirect" title="Bubbling Under the Hot 100">Bubbling Under the Hot 100</a>. The deluxe's second single, "Top Gone", was released on August 5, featuring Puerto Rican rapper <a href="/wiki/Lunay_(singer)" title="Lunay (singer)">Lunay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> On August 9, Mosey was included on the remix of <a href="/wiki/Past_Life_(Trevor_Daniel_song)" title="Past Life (Trevor Daniel song)">Past Life</a>, a single by American singer <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Daniel_(singer)" title="Trevor Daniel (singer)">Trevor Daniel</a>, which also features American singer <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a>. The deluxe edition of <i>Certified Hitmaker</i>, marketed as <i>Certified Hitmaker (AVA Leak)</i>, was released on August 14, 2020. It includes the two singles as well as three additional tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> On August 28, Mosey was featured on "Lost Me", the third track on American record label <a href="/wiki/Internet_Money" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet Money">Internet Money</a>'s debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/B4_the_Storm" title="B4 the Storm">B4 the Storm</a></i>, which also features fellow American rappers <a href="/wiki/Iann_Dior" title="Iann Dior">Iann Dior</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Skies" title="Lil Skies">Lil Skies</a>.
</p><p>On August 30, during an interview with The Hollywood Fix, Mosey teased a new project by playing a snippet of new music. The project was later announced to be a new mixtape titled <i>Universal</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape will act as a transition between <i>Certified Hitmaker</i>, and his upcoming third studio album: <i>The Land of Make Believe</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jumpin_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jumpin-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> On September 9, Mosey was included on the remix of "<a href="/wiki/Be_Happy_(Dixie_D%27Amelio_song)" title="Be Happy (Dixie D&#39;Amelio song)">Be Happy</a>", the debut single by American <a href="/wiki/Social_media_personality" class="mw-redirect" title="Social media personality">social media personality</a> <a href="/wiki/Dixie_D%27Amelio" title="Dixie D&#39;Amelio">Dixie D'Amelio</a>, which also features American singer <a href="/wiki/Blackbear_(musician)" title="Blackbear (musician)">blackbear</a>. On October 1, Mosey released a video on his YouTube channel celebrating the world premiere of <a href="/wiki/FIFA_21" title="FIFA 21">FIFA 21</a>, which doubles as the trailer for <i>Universal</i>. In it, Mosey wears a custom jersey and performs a medley of his songs "Bands Out Tha Roof", "Blueberry Faygo", and "Live This Wild", respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> A day later, Mosey was featured on "Thug Kry", a song on American rapper <a href="/wiki/YG_(rapper)" title="YG (rapper)">YG</a>'s fifth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/My_Life_4Hunnid" title="My Life 4Hunnid">My Life 4Hunnid</a></i>, which also features fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Calboy" title="Calboy">Calboy</a>. On October 21, Mosey was included on the remix of "<a href="/wiki/Lets_Link" title="Lets Link">Lets Link</a>", a song by American rapper WhoHeem, which also features fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Tyga" title="Tyga">Tyga</a>. On October 30, Mosey appeared on "No Honourable Mention", a song on American rapper <a href="/wiki/Trippie_Redd" title="Trippie Redd">Trippie Redd</a>'s third studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Pegasus_(Trippie_Redd_album)" title="Pegasus (Trippie Redd album)">Pegasus</a></i>, which also features fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Quavo" title="Quavo">Quavo</a>. This was notably their third official collaboration, after "Never Scared" and "This Ain't That". On November 6, Mosey released the single "Krabby Step" in collaboration with fellow American rappers <a href="/wiki/Tyga" title="Tyga">Tyga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swae_Lee" title="Swae Lee">Swae Lee</a> from the soundtrack for <i><a href="/wiki/The_SpongeBob_Movie:_Sponge_on_the_Run" title="The SpongeBob Movie: Sponge on the Run">The SpongeBob Movie: Sponge on the Run</a></i>. On November 13, 2020, Mosey released "Jumpin Out the Face", as the originally intended lead single for his upcoming mixtape <i>Universal</i>, along with an accompanying music video. One week later, Mosey was featured on "How We Doin It", a song on American rapper <a href="/wiki/French_Montana" title="French Montana">French Montana</a>'s mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/CB5" title="CB5">CB5</a></i>. The same day, Mosey was also featured on "Gangang", the penultimate track on Italian rapper <a href="/wiki/Sfera_Ebbasta" title="Sfera Ebbasta">Sfera Ebbasta</a>'s album <i>Famoso</i>. On December 4, Mosey was featured on "Bussin' Out", the fifth track on American producer DJ Scheme's debut studio album <i>FAMILY</i>, which also features American singer <a href="/wiki/Ty_Dolla_$ign" class="mw-redirect" title="Ty Dolla $ign">Ty Dolla $ign</a>. A week later, Mosey appeared on "Out The Mud", the third track on American rapper <a href="/wiki/Hotboii" title="Hotboii">Hotboii</a>'s debut studio album <i>Double O Baby</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2021-2022:_Delay_of_Universal_and_standalone_releases">2021-2022: Delay of <i>Universal</i> and standalone releases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2021-2022: Delay of Universal and standalone releases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To start of 2021, Mosey was featured on the remix of "Blueberry Eyes" on January 22, the 2020 hit single by American singer <a href="/wiki/Max_Schneider" title="Max Schneider">MAX</a>, which also features South Korean rapper <a href="/wiki/Suga_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Suga (rapper)">Suga</a> from <a href="/wiki/BTS" title="BTS">BTS</a> and American singer <a href="/wiki/Olivia_O%27Brien" title="Olivia O&#39;Brien">Olivia O'Brien</a>. On January 25, 2021, his nineteenth birthday, Mosey celebrated by releasing "Holy Water", as the second single for <i>Universal</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Four days later, Mosey was featured on "Boom Boom", the fourth track on the EP <i>Lucky 7</i> by American rapper <a href="/wiki/Rich_the_Kid" title="Rich the Kid">Rich the Kid</a>. On February 5, Mosey released "We Outside", a song in collaboration with fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Smokepurpp" title="Smokepurpp">Smokepurpp</a>. A week later, he released the album's third single, "Enough", which coincided with a Valentine's Day release.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On March 15, he released the fourth single, "Try Me". Its music video premiered the next day, and has been viewed over 13 million times. Soon after, on March 26, Mosey was featured on "<a href="/wiki/Jetski_(song)" title="Jetski (song)">Jetski</a>", a single by American record label <a href="/wiki/Internet_Money" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet Money">Internet Money</a>. The song also features fellow American rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Tecca" title="Lil Tecca">Lil Tecca</a>, with whom Mosey had been feuding with since 2019. Thus the song marked the squashing of their feud. Being <a href="/wiki/Internet_Money" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet Money">Internet Money</a>'s first single of 2021, an accompanying music video was released a day later on Internet Money's <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel, which has garnered over 20 million views to date. "<a href="/wiki/Jetski_(song)" title="Jetski (song)">Jetski</a>" peaked at number 19 on the US <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_the_Hot_100" class="mw-redirect" title="Bubbling Under the Hot 100">Bubbling Under the Hot 100</a> and number 88 on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a>, going on to become Mosey's most successful release post "Blueberry Faygo". After Mosey's rape allegations surfaced in April 2021, he took a three month hiatus from music, before returning with "How I Been" and "Problem Solvin" in July, which were two songs uploaded exclusively on his official <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel. Two months later on September 1, he released a standalone single "Pass Out". On November 9, Mosey uploaded a combined music video for "So Fast" and "Speed Racin", which were two songs from his second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Certified_Hitmaker" title="Certified Hitmaker">Certified Hitmaker</a></i>, to commemorate the album's two year anniversary. Mosey then released the single "Not The Same God As Mine" on December 10, as his first official single post-allegations. 
</p><p>This was followed up by multiple singles released in early 2022, including "Ain't It A Flex", "Falling", and "Breathin Again", which were all accompanied by music videos on Mosey's YouTube channel. On April 8, 2022, Mosey featured on the song "Gracias A Dios" from Mexican rapper Natanael Cano's album <i>NataKong</i>. On May 26, Mosey had a guest appearance on "Bipolar", a single by Argentine rapper <a href="/wiki/Lit_Killah" title="Lit Killah">Lit Killah</a>. On October 6, Mosey announced the release of an EP titled "UNI". The 3-track EP was released two weeks later on October 19, containing the songs "Paid Up", "Drop Top", and "Sick Today". All three songs were followed up with music videos on Mosey's <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel over the next two weeks. On November 7, Mosey announced the release of a second EP titled "VER". It was surprise released on November 29, containing three songs: "Backpack", "Matte Red/Sum He Said", and "Rocket". The music video for "Rocket" was released on November 30. The third and final EP of the series, "SAL", is expected to be released in early 2023. Its release date is currently unknown.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2023:_Universal_Rollout">2023: <i>Universal</i> Rollout</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2023: Universal Rollout">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On March 3, 2023, Mosey was acquitted of rape. On the same day, he posted on Instagram a snippet of the unreleased song "Flu Game", thanking God for bringing "the truth to light". It was released as a single two weeks later on March 17 with an accompanying music video premiering the next day. The music video received over 1 million views in less than 24 hours. "Flu Game" is expected to mark the rollout of <i>Universal</i>, which is likely to be released later this year.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Certified_Hitmakers_record_label">Certified Hitmakers record label</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Certified Hitmakers record label">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2020, Mosey opened his own record label Certified Hitmakers.
</p><p>His first signee was Jae Lynx, who released his debut single "Bad Girl Vibes" under the label on November 6, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> On January 14, 2021, Lynx released his second single "Regrets" with <a href="/wiki/YNW_BSlime" title="YNW BSlime">YNW BSlime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Musical style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lil Mosey is known for his melodic flow and lyrics that are tailored to his life.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> When asked if the term "<a href="/wiki/Mumble_rap" title="Mumble rap">mumble rap</a>" applies to him in an interview with Complex, Lil Mosey says "I wouldn't consider myself a mumble rapper, because I don't know what that is. But when I talk, I mumble."<sup id="cite_ref-:2_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Although Lil Mosey does not consider his sound to be similar to <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a>'s, he does consider the rapper an influence as in an interview with XXL Magazine, he describes how he would always listen to Meek Mill's song "Dreams and Nightmares" when he was younger.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> When asked in the same interview about what comparisons he has drawn, Mosey responded "Music-wise, they be comparing me to <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lil Mosey has toured with rappers Smooky MarGielaa, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Tjay" title="Lil Tjay">Lil Tjay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polo_G" title="Polo G">Polo G</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smokepurpp" title="Smokepurpp">Smokepurpp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, Lil Mosey was on tour with <a href="/wiki/Juice_Wrld" title="Juice Wrld">Juice Wrld</a> and <a href="/wiki/YBN_Cordae" class="mw-redirect" title="YBN Cordae">YBN Cordae</a>, serving as the opening act for Juice Wrld's WRLD Domination Tour.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He has also received a co-sign from <a href="/wiki/Lil_Xan" title="Lil Xan">Lil Xan</a>, and he says his first real live performance as an established artist came when Lil Xan brought him on stage during his concert in Seattle.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The rapper also performed at Rolling Loud in 2018. Lil Mosey has also toured with Sauve and Bandkidjay. He has given free performances, such as one in Seattle for a baby toy drive. He  toured Europe, Canada and the US on the Certified Hitmaker Tour.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rape_charge_and_trial">Rape charge and trial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Rape charge and trial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On April 2, 2021, Echols was charged with one count of <a href="/wiki/Rape_laws_in_the_United_States" title="Rape laws in the United States">second-degree rape</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lewis_County,_Washington" title="Lewis County, Washington">Lewis County, Washington</a>, for engaging in sexual intercourse with an individual that was incapable of giving consent.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:5_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He pleaded not guilty.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The charge stemmed from an alleged incident on the night of January 5, 2020, at a cabin in <a href="/wiki/Randle,_Washington" title="Randle, Washington">Randle, Washington</a>, where Echols had hosted a party.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Echols was not an adult at the time of the alleged incident, as he turned 18 on January 25, 2020. In accordance with a pre-trial sexual assault <a href="/wiki/Restraining_order" title="Restraining order">protective order</a>, Echols was ordered not to contact or come within 500 feet of the victim, and was prohibited from possessing firearms or using drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Echols faced a minimum of 78 to 102 months and a maximum of <a href="/wiki/Life_imprisonment_in_the_United_States" title="Life imprisonment in the United States">life in prison</a> if convicted.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:6_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Echols was tried in a <a href="/wiki/Joinder" title="Joinder">joint trial</a> alongside co-defendants Francisco P. Prater and Joshua D. Darrow. Prater was also accused of also raping the woman and Darrow was accused of restraining the alleged victim as Echols and Prater allegedly raped her.<sup id="cite_ref-July_18_trial_date_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-July_18_trial_date-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alleged_incident">Alleged incident</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Alleged incident">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Upon being contacted by the <a href="/wiki/Morton,_Washington" title="Morton, Washington">Morton</a> Police Department on January 6, 2020, the alleged victim told a detective that she attended the party with a friend and <a href="/wiki/Blackout_(drug-related_amnesia)" title="Blackout (drug-related amnesia)">blacked out</a> after drinking <a href="/wiki/White_Claw_Hard_Seltzer" title="White Claw Hard Seltzer">White Claw</a> alcoholic beverages and <a href="/wiki/Champagne" title="Champagne">champagne</a> provided at the party. The woman stated that she could not clearly remember the events of the rest of the night, and could only remember walking in her underwear to an upstairs bedroom, being told by individuals that she had sex, and being told that there was video recording of the intercourse. However, she had no memory of the rape. She stated that upon waking up the following morning, she and the friend she came with left the cabin.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 9, 2020, the Morton Police Department interviewed the woman's friend, who stated that she had consensual sex with Echols in his car, during which she felt a pain in her legs. She stated that she had a "fuzzy" memory of what happened afterwards, but that the next thing she remembered was multiple men forcing themselves onto her, including a man identified as Francisco P. Prater saying "wake up, wake up, suck this dick, bitch." Prater was also charged with one count of second-degree rape, in tandem with Echols' rape charge.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> She also claimed that she had bruises on her arm, neck, and inner knee that she did not know the origin of. In a later interview with police, the woman alleged that she remembered waking up to Echols raping her in an upstairs bedroom after she had blacked out.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trial_and_acquittal">Trial and acquittal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lil_Mosey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Trial and acquittal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On April 21, 2021, a $50,000 <a href="/wiki/Arrest_warrant#United_States" title="Arrest warrant">warrant</a> was issued for Echols' arrest after he failed to show up for a required court appearance at a preliminary hearing.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:6_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> After a deal was made between Echols and the Lewis County Prosecutor's Office to quash the warrant, Echols appeared in court on April 27.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> On July 13, Echols appeared at a pre-trial <a href="/wiki/Omnibus_hearing" title="Omnibus hearing">omnibus hearing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Third_defendant_named_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Third_defendant_named-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Prater was also charged with one count of second-degree rape in tandem with Echols' rape charge.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:8_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Joshua D. Darrow was named as a third defendant in the rape case in July 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-Third_defendant_named_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Third_defendant_named-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Darrow was released on unsecured bail and was also issued a pre-trial sexual assault protective order.<sup id="cite_ref-Third_defendant_named_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Third_defendant_named-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the trial, Echols was out on $50,000 unsecured bail.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The joint trial alongside co-defendants Prater and Darrow was expected to begin on January 24, 2022, which was then delayed to July 18, then again delayed to December 12, and then set for February 16, 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-Third_defendant_named_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Third_defendant_named-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-July_18_trial_date_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-July_18_trial_date-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-February_16_trial_date_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-February_16_trial_date-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Echols reportedly passed a <a href="/wiki/Polygraph_test" class="mw-redirect" title="Polygraph test">polygraph test</a>. The trial began on February 22, 2023. On March 2, 2023, Echols was found <a href="/wiki/Acquittal" title="Acquittal">not guilty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-upper-alpha">

<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Not be confused with his 2018 album <i><a href="/wiki/Northsbest" title="Northsbest">Northsbest</a></i>, this is a self released mixtape with the same name but is a different project entirely.</span>
